Jamison Brereton

33 (224)
Rudra
Gr╠еtsamada
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
Although under his transferred epithet ┼Ъiva (тАЬkindly oneтАЭ), Rudra has a grand career ahead of him in post-Vedic Hinduism, his role in Vedic, especially early Vedic, is relatively restrained. Only three complete R╠еgvedic hymns are dedi cated to him (I.114 and VII.46, in addition to this one, as well as two hymns conjointly dedicated to Rudra and Soma, I.43 and VI.74). He is known espe cially as the father of the Maruts, and he has a dual nature: on the one hand, he is prone to anger and quick to dispatch his weapons, especially his arrows, at those who enrage him; on the other, he is a provider of healing remedies and of good luck.
The major part of this hymn is devoted to begging the god Rudra for his indul gence and his healing powers, but it also nervously expresses the hope that his venge ful assaults will be directed elsewhere. The dual nature of Rudra as both healer and avenger is thus on display, and his parentage of the Maruts begins the hymn (vs. 1) and is mentioned several times in the course of it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Rudra This is a much anthologized hymn, fully translated by Macdonell in VRS, Doniger, and Maurer. Its popularity is not surprising: itтАЩs lively and varied, but does not pose major difficulties, though it has its share of small knots.

Renou EVP XV.157-60.

рд╣реЗрдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореНрдкрд┐рддрдГ рдорд░реБрддреНрд╕рдЮреНрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдиреНрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореБрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХрд░реБрджреНрд░ рдкрд░рдордкрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реАрддрд┐рд╖рд╖реНрдареНрдпрдиреНрддрд╕реНрдпрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рддрд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╡ рджреНрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рддреНрд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рддреЗрддреНрд╡рджреАрдпрдВ рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╕реБрдореНрдирдВрд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдЖрдПрддреБрдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ рд░реБрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрдЪ рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореНрдкрд┐рддреГ рддреНрд╡рдорд┐рджрдореНрдкрд┐рддреНрд░реЗрдорд░реБрддрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрддреНрд░рд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрд┐рдХрд╛рдореБрдЦреЗрдирд╛рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реНрдо рддрдерд╛рддреНрд╡рдиреНрдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдиреНрджреГрд╢рдГ рд╕рдиреНрджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рдиреНрдорд╛рдпреБ- рдпреЛрдерд╛рдГ рдорд╛рдкреГрдердХреНрдХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реАрдГ рдпреБрдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рдгрд╛рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рдгрдпреЛрдГ рд▓рдЩрд┐рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдГрд╢рдкрдГрд╢реНрд▓реБрдГ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпреБрднрдпрдереЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдзрдзрд╛рддреБрдХрддреНрд╡реЗрди- рдЩрд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреНрдЧреБрдгрдГ рдЕрд░реНрд╡рддрд┐рд╢рддреНрд░реМ рднреНрд░рд╛рддрд╡реНрдпреЛрд╡рд╛рдЕрд░реНрд╡реЗрддрд┐рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ ред рдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВрд╡реАрд░рдГ рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдХреНрд╖- рдореЗрдд рдЕрднрд┐рднрд╡рддреБ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реМ рд╡реАрд░рд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЕрднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореЗрдерд╛рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреНрдХреГрддрд╛рдкрд░рд╛рдзрд╛рдиреН рдЕрднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рдорд╕реНрд╡ рд╣реЗрд░реБрджреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдкреМрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдпреЗрдорд╣рд┐ рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрд╛рдГрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рее рез рее

English translation:

тАЬFather of the MarutsтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Idam pitre marut─Бm: RV 1.114.6], may the felicity extend to us; exclude us not from the sight of the sun; (grant that) our valiant (descendants) may overcome (these) foes, and that we may be multiplied, Rudra, by (our) progeny.

Jamison Brereton

Let your favor come here, o father of the Maruts. Do not keep us away from the sight of the sun.
The hero on horseback should be indulgent. Might we be further
propagated through our offspring, Rudra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The only difficult p─Бda is c, which has received a variety of interpr. The first question is whether v─лr├│ ├бrvati should be construed together or ├бrvati taken with some other part of the clause. With Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) I take the two words together in the published translation; most other tr. (Macdonell, Renou, Doniger, Maurer) take it with naс╕е or directly with the verb abh├н тАж kс╣гameta. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take the hero to be one of us, a human; this leads Geldner to interpr. the verb as passive (тАЬEs m├╢ge unser Kriegsmann zu Ross verschont bliebenтАЭ), although all forms of this idiom, med. abh├н тИЪkс╣гam, all of which appear in this little group of hymns (II.28.3, 29.2, 33.1, 33.7), have the same meaning, тАЬbe indulgent/patient towardsтАЭ (see esp. vs. 7). With most tr. I instead understand v─лr├б- to be Rudra; it is appropriate to ask for his indulgence or patience.

This leads us to the question of whether Rudra is likely to be on horseback. I know of no evidence for or against, but given that Rudra is the MarutsтАЩ father and they are often associated with horses, it is certainly possible. However, the only other occurrence of ├бrvati in the RV (VIII.71.12) appears to be an unmarked loc. absolute: we ask Agni for help тАЬwhen a charger (is at stake).тАЭ It is therefore possible that the same usage is found here, and the p─Бda should mean тАЬThe hero should be indulgent to us when a charger (is at stake).тАЭ I leave the question open.

Griffith

FATHER of Maruts, let thy bliss approach us: exclude us not from looking on the sunlight.
Gracious to our fleet courser be the Hero may we transplant us, Rudra, in our children.

Macdonell

Let thy goodwill, O father of the Maruts, Light on us: part us not from S┼лrya’s vision. In mercy may the hero spare our horses: May we, O Rudra, have abundant offspring.

Geldner

Deine Huld soll kommen, du Vater der Marut, verwehr uns nicht den Anblick der Sonne ! Es m├╢ge unser Kriegsmann zu Ro├Я verschont bleiben. Wir m├╢chten uns durch deine Kinder fortpflanzen, o Rudra.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рддреЗ) рддрд╡ (рдкрд┐рддрдГ) рдкрд┐рддреГрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк (рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН (рд╕реБрдореНрдирдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрдореН (рдПрддреБ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ (рдорд╛) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпреЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп (рд╕рдВрджреГрд╢рдГ) рдпрдГ рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рдкрд╢реНрдпрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдп (рдпреБрдпреЛрдерд╛рдГ) рдкреГрдердХреН рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ (рдЕрднрд┐) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╡реАрд░рдГ) рд╢реБрднрдЧреБрдгрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреА (рдЕрд░реНрд╡рддрд┐) рдЙрддреНрддрдореЗрд╜рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ (рдХреНрд╖рдореЗрдд) рд╕рд╣реЗрдд (рдкреНрд░) (рдЬрд╛рдпреЗрдорд╣рд┐) (рд░реБрджреНрд░) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд░реЛрджрдпрд┐рддрдГ (рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ реерезрее

English translation:

тАЬNourished by the curative vegetables which are bestowed by you, may I live a hundred winters; extirpate mine enemies, my exceeding sin, and my manifold infirmities.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Through the remedies given by you that bring best luck, Rudra, might I reach a hundred winters.
Banish hatred away from us, very far away, distress away, and afflictions away, widely scattered.

Griffith

With the most saving medicines which thou givest, Rudra, may I attain a hundred winters.
Far from us banish enmity and hatred, and to all quarters maladies and trouble.

Macdonell

By thy most wholesome remedies, O Rudra, Thy gifts, I would attain a hundred autumns. Drive far away from us distress and hatred, Drive far away, wide-scattered, all diseases.

Geldner

Durch deine heilsamsten Arzeneien, die du gibst, o Rudra, m├╢chte ich hundert Winter erleben. Jage die Anfeindungen, die Not weit weg von uns, treib die Krankheiten auseinander!

Grassmann

Lass mich durch deine besten Arzeneien, o Rudra, hundert Jahre noch erleben; Vertreib weit von uns hinweg die Feindschaft, nach allen Seiten Siechthum und Bedr├дngniss.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Rudra, are the chief of beings in glory; you, wielder of the thunderbolt, are the might of themighty; do you waft us in safety over (the ocean) of sin; repel all the assaults of iniquity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

In glory you are the most glorious of anyone born, Rudra, the most powerful of the powerful, o you with the mace in your arms.
Take us across to the far shore of distress, to well-being. Keep away all assaults of malady.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is the only occurrence of sg. v├бjra-b─Бhu- that doesnтАЩt qualify Indra.

(The only non-sg. form is dual vajra-b─Бh┼л addressed to Indra and Agni in I.109.7.) I do not know why Rudra is thus identified here.

Chief of all born art thou in glory, Rudra, armed with the thunder, mightiest of the mighty.
Transport us over trouble to well-being repel thou from us all assaults of mis. chief.

Of what is born thou art the chief in glory, Armed with the thunder, mightiest of the mighty. Transport us to the farther shore of trouble In safety; frustrate all attacks of mischief.

рд╣реЗрд░реБрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрдирдореЛрднрд┐рдГ рдЕрдпрдерд╛рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгреИрд░реНрдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░реИрдГ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдорд╛рдЪреБрдХреНрд░реБрдзрд╛рдо рдорд╛рдХреНрд░реЛрдзрдпрд╛рдо рдХреНрд░реБрджреНрдзрдВ рдорд╛рдХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реНрдо рдХреНрд░реБрдзрдХреЛрдкреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдгреНрдпрдиреНрддрд╛рд▓реНрд▓реБрдЩрд┐рдЪрдЩрд┐рд░реВрдкрдореН рд╣реЗрд╡реГрд╖рдн рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВрд╡рд░реНрд╖рд┐рддрдГ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрддреА рджреБрдГрд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд╢реЛ- рднрдирдпрд╛рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╛ рдорд╛рдЪреБрдХреНрд░реБрдзрд╛рдореЗрддреНрдпреЗрд╡ рддрдерд╛ рд░рд╣реВрддреА рд╕рд╣реВрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╕рджреГрд╢реИрд░рдиреНрдпреИрд░реНрджреЗрд╡реИрдГ рд╕рд╣рд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдиреЗрдирдорд╛рдХреНрд░реЛрдзрдпрд╛рдо рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдареЛрд╣рд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдиреНрдпреВрдиреЗрдирд╕рд╣рд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдиреЗрдХреНрд░реБрджреНрдзреЛрднрд╡рддрд┐ рд╕рддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВрд╡реАрд░рд╛рдиреН рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН рднреЗрд╖рдЬреЗрднрд┐рдГ рддреНрд╡рджреАрдпреИрд░реНрднреЗрд╖рдЬреИрд░реМрд╖рдзреИрдГ рдЙрджрд░реНрдкрдп рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдВрд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЬрдп рд╣реЗрд░реБрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореНрднрд┐рд╖рдЬрд╛рдЮреНрдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╕рд╛рднрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдореНрдордзреНрдпреЗрднрд┐рд╖рдХреНрддрдордВ рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрдирднреИрд╖рдЬреНрдпрд╕реНрдп- рдХрд░реНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╢реНрд░реГрдгреЛрдорд┐ рдкреНрд░рдердореЛрджреИрд╡реНрдпреЛрднрд┐рд╖рдЧрд┐рддрд┐рдЪрдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗрдкреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН рее рек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet us not provoke you, Rudra, to wrath by our (imperfect) adorations; nor, showerer (of benefits), by our unworthy praise, nor by our invocation (of other deities); invigorate our sons by your medicinal plural nts, for I hear that you are a chief physician amongst physicians.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bhiс╣гaktamam tv─Б bhiс╣гaj─Бm ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зomi: an emphatic attribution of qualities of a physician to Rudra

Jamison Brereton

Let us not anger you, Rudra, through our acts of reverence, nor through poor praise, nor through an invocation shared (with other gods),
o bull.
Set up our heroes with your remedies: I hear that you are the best healer of healers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The s├бh┼лti-, a joint invocation (with another god or gods), may be a sore subject for Rudra. As pointed out in the published introduction, he receives only three hymns dedicated to him alone in the RV; otherwise two hymns joint with Soma and incidental mentions in hymns to other gods. He may feel slighted. See also disc. ad VI.49.10.

Griffith

Let us not anger thee with worship, Rudra, ill praise, Strong God! or mingled invocation.
Do thou with strengthening balms incite our heroes: I hear thee famed as best of all physicians.

Macdonell

May we not anger thee with homage, Rudra, Nor with ill-praises, nor joint invocation. Raise up, O Bull, with remedies our heroes: I hear of thee as best of all physicians.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay I pacify by my praises that Rudra, who is worshipped with invocations and oblations; and never may he who is soft-bellied, of a tawny hue, and handsome chin; who is reverently invoked; subject us to that malevolent disposition (that purposes our destruction).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Soft-bellied: с╣Ыd┼лdara babhruvarс╣Зa su┼Ыipra: с╣Ыd┼лdara = mс╣Ыdu udara, having a soft belly (Nirukta 6.4); that malevolent disposition: m─Б no asyai r─лradhan man─Бyai: man─Б = hann─лti manyam─Бn─Б buddhiс╕е, the mind meditating, I kill

Jamison Brereton

Whoever invokes him with invocations and offerings, (thinking,) тАЬWith my praises might I cut off Rudra as my own exclusive portion,тАЭ
to the zeal (of this person) let the red-brown one with powerful lips
[=Rudra] not subordinate usтАФ(Rudra) being tender-hearted and easy to invoke.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I am in agreement with most tr. (though not Macdonell) that p─Бda b is the thought of the subject of the rel. cl. in p─Бda a, namely the over-zealous sacrificer. The verb ├бva тАж diс╣г─лya belongs not with тИЪd─Б тАШgiveтАЩ (with Grassmann), but тИЪd─Б тАШcut, divideтАЩ (so already Wh Roots); see esp. Narten (Sig Aor. 138-40). The idiom ├бva тИЪd─Б is generally taken, including by Narten, to mean тАШabfindenтАЩ (propitiate, compensate), but I think it has a more literal meaning here, тАШcut offтАЩ. The too-little ritual service of vs. 4 – poor praise (d├║с╣гс╣нuti-) and shared invocation (s├бh┼лti-) – meets the contrasting fault in vs. 5: the over-eager worshiper who wants Rudra as his own exclusively. This is a dramatic opposite of the s├бh┼лti-; not only an invocation directed only to this god, but one not jointly produced by the group of priests and worshippers. Such a private oneon-one human-divine relationship would be quite anomalous in the RVic religious world, where divine service requires cooperation among various ritual personnel.

The personal appeals in the Vasiс╣гс╣нha-Varuс╣Зa hymns of VII have such a strong impact in part because they deviate so far from ordinary religious practice.

The standard interpr. of the second hemistich makes the main clause rather loosely attached to the rel. cl. of p─Бda a. The тАЬusтАЭ (naс╕е) of c is supposed to pick up the y├бс╕е of a and the man─Б╠Б- of d is supposed to refer rather vaguely to the sentiment expressed in ab: in other words, we donтАЩt want to be the sort of person who might think such a thing or be suspected of thinking such a thing. I think the connection is much simpler. man─Б╠Б- is generally тАШzealтАЩ or тАШenthusiasmтАЩ; it is not inherently a negative notion, but becomes negative in the wrong hands (or mind). In my interpr., the тАЬwhoeverтАЭ of the rel. cl. in a is our sacrificial rival, who is trying to cut us out of the deal, as it were, by getting Rudra to himself. We beg Rudra not to make us subject to, subordinate to, his over-zealous action.

The epithet с╣Ыd┼лd├бra- тАШtender-heartedтАЩ is a charming phonetic play on RudraтАЩs name, which is almost always read trisyllabically (rudara) in this hymn.

Another adj. (see 3b above) otherwise used (almost) exclusively of Indra: su┼Ы├нpra- тАШwell-lippedтАЩ (of Agni V.22.4; in pl. of с╣Ъbhukс╣гans VII.37.1).

Griffith

May I with praise-songs win that Rudra’s favour who is adored with gifts and invocations.
Ne’er may the tawny God, fair-checked, and gracious, swifthearing, yield us to this evil purpose.

Macdonell

With invocations and oblations summoned Rudra I would appease with my laudations: May he, soft-hearted, easily appealed to, Brown-hued, fair-lipped, not to his wrath subject us.

Geldner

Wer mit Anrufungen, mit Opfergaben ihn ruft, indem er denkt: ich m├╢chte den Rudra mit Lobliedern abfinden - Solchem Verdacht m├╢ge uns der mildherzige, leicht zu errufende, rotbraune Rudra mit der sch├╢nen Lippe nicht preisgeben.

Grassmann

Der durch Gebet sich rufen l├дsst und Opfer, den Rudra will mit Liedern ich bes├дnft’gen; Nicht geb’ uns seinem Zorne hin der milde, geneigte, braune mit dem sch├╢nen Helme.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the showerer of benefits, the lord of the Maruts, gratify me his suppliant with invogorating food; may I, free from sin, so propitiate Rudra, that I may attain to his felicity, as a man, distressed by heat, (finds relief) in the shade.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The bull, in the company of the Maruts, roused me up when I was in need, with his more energetic vitality.
Free of malady, might I reach (this), like shade during the heat: might I attract here the favor of Rudra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ghс╣Ы╠Бс╣З─л see Oldenberg

I take тАШfavorтАЩ (sumn├бm) as the gapped goal of the verb in c, a┼Ы─лya тАШmight I reachтАЩ.

Griffith

The Strong, begirt by Maruts, hath refreshed me, with most invigorating food, imploring.
As he who finds a shade in fervent sunlight may I, uninjured, win the bliss of Rudra.

Macdonell

The bull, escorted by the Maruts, gladdens Me who invokes, with his most forceful vigour. I, sound, would reach, as in the heat, a shelter: Rudra’s good will I would desire to capture.

Geldner

Begeistert hat mich der Bulle mit der Marutschar durch seine starke Kraft, mich den Schutzbed├╝rftigen. Ohne Gebreste m├╢chte ich sie wie den Schatten in der Sonnenglut erreichen: des Rudra Gnade m├╢chte ich zu gewinnen suchen.

Grassmann

Erfreut hat mich der Held mit seinen Marut’s mit gr├╢ss’rer Kraft, als ich um H├╝lfe flehte; Wie Schatten vor der Glut m├╢g’ unversehrt ich des Rudra Huld erreichen und gewinnen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhere, Rudra, is your joy-dispending hand, which is the healer and delighter (of all); showerer (of benefits), who are the dispeller of sins of the gods, quickly have compassion upon me.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The dispeller of the sins of the gods: apabhart─Б rapaso daivyasya = devakс╣Ыtasya p─Бpasya apahart─Б, the taker-away of sin committed by a divinity; daivya may also connote sin against the gods

Jamison Brereton

Where, o Rudra, is that merciful hand of yours, which is a healing remedy,
the bearer away of malady that comes from the gods? You should now be indulgent toward me, o bull.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b the y├│ ├бsti тАж clause might appear to be embedded in the main clause, if c resumes the question posed in a. However, c could simply be part of the rel. cl.

Even if b is embedded, it is unproblematic, since nominal rel. clauses are an exception to the no-embedding rule, functioning rather like izafe-s.

In d abh─л╠БтАж cakс╣гam─лth─Бс╕е reprises 1c abh├н тАж kс╣гameta. Given that final lengthening in the preverb abh├н is extremely rare (Lubotsky: 739 abh├н, 14 abh─л╠Б.), I am inclined to interpr. the form as abh├н ─л, with the enclitic acc. anticipating the obj. m─Б, esp. given that in vs. 1 in this same idiom abh├н appears without length.

Griffith

Where is that gracious hand of thine, O Rudra, the hand that giveth health and bringeth comfort,
Remover of the woe that Gods have sent us? O Strong One, look thou on me with compassion.

Macdonell

Where is that gracious hand of thine, O Rudra, That is so full of remedies and coolness? As the remover of all god-sent damage, Do thou, O Bull, now show compassion towards me.

Geldner

Wo ist, Rudra, diese deine mildt├дtige Hand, die heilend, k├╝hlend ist, die das von G├╢ttern kommende Gebreste fortnimmt ? Du solltest doch mit mir Nachsicht haben, du Bulle!

Grassmann

Wo ist, o Rudra, deine Hand, die milde, die Heilung schafft und alle Schmerzen lindert, Die auch hinwegnimmt gottverh├дngte Krankheit; jetzt ├╝b’ Erbarmen gegen mich, o Starker.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI address infinite and earnest praise to the showerer (of benefits), the cherisher (of all), the white-complexioned; adore the consumer (of sin), with prostrations; we glorify the illustrious name of Rudra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

White-complexioned: ┼Ыvit─лce = ┼Ыvaityam a├▒cate, he who goes to or obtains whiteness

Jamison Brereton

To the red-brown, bright-faced bull, I rouse forth greatly a great good praise hymn.
I shall do reverence to the sparkling one with acts of reverence. We sing the turbulent name of Rudra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb in c, namasy─Б╠Б, can be either 2nd sg. impv. or 1st sg. subj., and translations differ. Because of the surrounding 1st ps. verbs (b: 1st sg. ─лray─Бmi, d: 1st pl. gс╣Ыс╣З─лm├бsi) I opt for the 1st sg. subjunctive, though there are no implications either way. kalmal─лk├нn- is obviously a possessive -├нn-stem built to a -ka-suffixed form of kalmal├н-, found once in the AV (XV.2.1-4) in unclear meaning, as descriptor of a jewel. The lтАЩs and the reduplicative rhyming formation (kal-mal-) mark it as nonstandard and suggest that it is affective in some fashion. My tr. тАЬsparkling oneтАЭ is similar to those of others, but given the uncertainty of the word and its base, it should have been marked with a question mark.

Griffith

To him the strong, great, tawny, fair-complexioned, I utter forth a mighty hymn of praises.
We serve the brilliant God with adorations, we glorify, the splendid name of Rudra.

Macdonell

Forth for the brown and whitish bull I utter A mighty panegyric of the mighty. I will adore the radiant god with homage. We praise the terrifying name of Rudra.

Geldner

Auf den rotbraunen, wei├Я angetanen Bullen, den hohen, hebe ich ein hohes Loblied an. Verneige dich vor dem Strahlenden mit Verbeugungen ! Wir preisen den furchtgebietenden Namen des Rudra.

Grassmann

Dem braunen Stiere, ihm dem sch├╢ngeschm├╝ckten, lass froh ein grosses Loblied ich erschallen; Den funkelnden verehrend mit Verehrung, erheben wir des Rudra hehren Namen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Firm) with strong limbs, assuming many forms fierce, and tawny-coloured, he shines with brilliant golden ornaments; vigour is inseparable from Rudra, the supreme ruler and lord of this world.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vigour: asuryam = bala, strength; or, it may connect Rudra with the asuras

Jamison Brereton

With sturdy limbs, the mighty red-brown one of many forms has adorned himself with gleaming golden (ornaments).
From Rudra, who is master over the abundant living world, lordly
power will surely not be distant.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tr. should be slight adjusted to тАЬthis тАж world,тАЭ to reflect the adjectival demonst. asy├б.

Griffith

With firm limbs, multiform, the strong, the tawny adorns himself with bright gold decorations:
The strength of Godhead ne’er departs from Rudra, him who is Sovran of this world, the mighty.

Macdonell

He, mighty, brown-hued, multiform, has decked out His stalwart limbs with jewels bright and golden, From Rudra, this great universe’s ruler, Let not be severed his divine dominion.

Geldner

Mit festen Gliedern, vielfarbig hat sich der Rotbraune, Gewaltige mit leuchtendem Goldschmuck geschm├╝ckt. Von dem Herrscher dieser gro├Яen Welt, von Rudra trennt sich f├╝rwahr nie die Asuraw├╝rde.

Mit starken Gliedern hat der m├дcht’ge, braune, und blankem Gold geschm├╝ckt sich vielgestaltig; Von ihm, der diese weite Welt beherrschet, von Rudra weichet nie die Lebensf├╝lle.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWorthy (of reverence), you bear arrows and a bow; worthy (of praise), you wear an adorable and omniform necklace; worthy (of adoration), you preseve all this vast universe; there is no one more powerful than you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Worship of reverence: arhan = arha, yogya, fit for, or worthy of;

Necklace: niс╣гka = h─Бra

Jamison Brereton

Worthily you bear the arrows and the bow and worthily the sacrificial neck ornament of all forms.
Worthily you parcel out the whole formless void. Surely there exists nothing more powerful than you, Rudra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Given that the two words for тАШbowтАЩ, dh├бnus- and dh├бnvan-, are suppletive in the RV with the former supplying the nom./acc. sg. and the latter the rest of the paradigm (see disc. ad VI.75.2), my tr. of dh├бnv─Б╠Ж(and indeed the various tr. of Renou, Macdonell, Doniger, and Maurer; GeldnerтАЩs тАЬtr├дgst du Pfeile und BogenтАЭ is ambiguous, because Bogen is both sg. and pl.) as singular must be wrong, and GrassmannтАЩs identification of the form as pl. is correct. In fact, though the Pp reads dh├бnva with short final, in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text the word spans the p─Бda boundary and coalesces with the following word as dh├бnv─Б╠Бrhann and so could be underlyingly dh├бnv─Б, with an unambig. pl. ending. In any case I would alter the published translation to тАЬarrows and bows.тАЭ The VP in c, id├бс╣Г dayase v├н┼Ыvam ├бbhvam, is variously rendered: Geldner тАЬverf├╝gst du ├╝ber all diese Gewalt,тАЭ Macdonell тАЬwieldest all this forceтАЭ (sim. Doniger, Maurer) versus Renou тАЬtu d├йtruis tout mal-informe,тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н тАЬтАж zerst├╢rst du all dieses Unwesen.тАЭ I do not think either of these approaches is correct. On the one hand, ├бbhva- does not mean тАШpowerтАЩ, but rather тАШformless(ness)тАЩ, often conceived as monstrous (RenouтАЩs тАШmalinformeтАЩ [badly shapeless], though odd, seems close). Nor does dayate, if belonging to тИЪd─Б тАШcut, divide, distributeтАЩ as Geldner et al. seem to take it, mean тАШwield, have controlтАЩ. As for the other view, Renou simply states that d├бyate can mean тАШdestroyтАЩ, while Witzel Got┼Н explicitly adopt Got┼НтАЩs view (1st class pres., 172-74) that there are two distinct roots тИЪd─Б that have d├бyate as pres., one тАШdivide, distributeтАЩ, the other тАШdestroyтАЩ. None of the passages adduced by Got┼Н for тАШdestroyтАЩ requires segregation in a separate root that has little else to support its existence; they can all be seen as metaphorical extensions of тАШdivide, cut apartтАЩ (3 of the 5 passages occur with v├н), an extension well within the bounds of RVic poetic imagination (though perhaps not of all its commentators). My own view is that the action attributed to Rudra here is a cosmogonic one, regularly performed by other Rigvedic gods, namely the division of the formless chaos of the pre-creation universe into what will later be referred to by the expression тАЬname-and-formтАЭ (n─Бma-r┼лpa-) As I have discussed in numerous other places (see, e.g., my forthcoming тАЬThe Blob in Ancient IndiaтАЭ), the Vedic conception of creation involves division into separate entities, with clear boundaries and names, of an originally fuzzy boundary-less mass, which strikes horror in the hearts of Vedic people. In my view, the verb dayate here has its standard root meaning, тАШcut, divide, apportionтАЩ, and Rudra is engaged in cosmogonic division. In this sense the verb often occurs with the preverb v├н, which sometimes occurs directly after the verb occupying post-caesura position (e.g. тАж d├бyase v├н тАж VI.37.4, VII.23.4). Although the preverb is not found here, v├н┼Ыvam immediately follows the verb and evokes the preverb. Note a different use of the same root in vs. 5; also note that n─Б╠Бma is found in 8d and -r┼лpa- in 9a, evoking the notion тАЬname and form.тАЭ In my publ tr. I did not fully render the id├бm, however. I would substitute тАЬthis whole formless voidтАЭ or perhaps тАЬthe whole formless void here.тАЭ

Griffith

Worthy, thou carriest thy bow and arrows, worthy, thy manyhued and honoured necklace.
Worthy, thou cuttest here each fiend to pieces: a mightier than thou there is not, Rudra.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorify the renowned Rudra, riding in his car, ever youthful, destructive, fierce like a formidable wild beast; Rudra, propitiated by praise, grant happiness to him who praises (you), and let your hosts destroy him who is our adversary.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Praise the famed youth, sitting upon the high seat, the mighty one, pouncing like a terrifying wild beast.
Being praised, have mercy on the singer, Rudra. Let your weapons cast down another than us.

Keith

Praise [3] the famous youth, mounted on the chariot seat, Dread and destructive like a fierce wild beast;
Being praised, O Rudra, be merciful to the singer; Let thy missiles smite down another than us.

Griffith

Praise him the chariot-borne, the young, the famous, fierce, slaying like a dread beast of the forest.
O Rudra, praised, be gracious to the singer. let thy hosts spare us and smite down another.

Macdonell

Praise him the famed, who sits upon the car-seat The young, the fierce, like a dread beast, a slayer. When praised, be gracious, Rudra, to the singer Let thy darts pass us and lay low another.

Geldner

Grassmann

Sing’ dem ber├╝hmten, jungen Wagenk├дmpfer, der kr├дftig angreift, wie ein grimmer L├╢we; Sei hold dem S├дnger, Rudra, du gelobter; dein Pfeil vernichte andere als wir sind.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╡рдиреНрджрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЖрдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдиреНрднрд╡рд╕реМрдореНрдпреЗрд╕реНрддреБрд╡рдиреНрддрдореНрдкрд┐рддрд░рдВ рдХреБрдорд╛рд░рд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рдпрдерд╛рдХреБрдорд╛рд░рдГ рдЪрд┐рджрд┐рддреНрдпреЗрддреНрджреБрдкрдорд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рд╣реЗрд░реБрджреНрд░ рдЙрдк- рдпрдиреНрддрдорд╕реНрдорддреНрд╕рдореАрдкреЗрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдиреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рдореНрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирдирд╛рдо рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирддреЛрд╕реНрдорд┐ рдЕрдкрд┐рдЪ рднреВрд░реЗрд░реНрдмрд╣реБрдиреЛрдзрдирд╕реНрдпрджрд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВрд╕рддреНрдкрддрд┐рдВрд╕рддрд╛рдореНрдкрд╛- рд▓рдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдкрддреНрдпрд╛рд╡реИрд╢рд░реНрдпреЗрдЗрддрд┐рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдкрджрдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рддреНрд╡рдореН рд╣реЗрд░реБрджреНрд░ рдПрд╡рдореНрднреВрддрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдЩреНрдЧреГрдгреАрд╖реЗ рд╕реНрддреМрдорд┐ рдорд┐рдкрд╕реНрддрд┐рдЩрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдЩреЛрдн- рд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐рд╕реЗрдЖрджреЗрд╢рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡рдВрдЕрд╕реНрдореЗрдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореНрднреЗрд╖рдЬрд╛рднреЗрд╖рдЬрд╛рдирд┐рд░рд╛рд╕рд┐рджреЗрд╣рд┐ рее резреи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI bow, Rudra, to you, approaching (our rite), as a boy to his father when pronouncing a blessing upon him; I glorify you, the giver of much (wealth), the protector of the virtuous; do you, thus glorified, bestow healing herbs upon me.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Even a little boy bows in response to his approving father as he approaches, o Rudra.
I will hymn the giver of much, the master of settlements. Praised,
bestow on us your remedies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although most tr. (Geldner, Renou, Doniger, Maurer, but not Macdonell) take n─Бn─Бma as 1st sg., with nom. kum─Бr├бс╕е relegated to a simile, I follow K├╝mmel (278)(and Macdonell, see also Grassmann) in taking n─Бn─Бma as 3rd sg. For one thing, cid isnтАЩt a simile particle (pace Geldner), and so this would have to be an unmarked simile (not, of course, impossible), and for another we might expect (or at least hope for) *n─Бnama with short root vowel as a 1st sg. pf. The point of the half-vs. must be that even a little boy knows to honor someone more powerful and distinguished than he is, and so I surely know to do the same.

Griffith

I bend to thee as thou approachest, Rudra, even as a boy before the sire who greets him.
I praise thee Bounteous Giver, Lord of heroes: give medicines to us as thou art lauded.

Macdonell

I bow down like a son before his father, Who with good will comes nigh to him, O Rudra. I praise the true lord, of much wealth the giver: To us thou grantest remedies when lauded.

Geldner

Wie der Knabe gegen den lobenden Vater, so habe ich mich gegen dich, Rudra, verneigt, wenn du nahst. Den Geber von vielem, den rechtm├д├Яigen Herrn feiere ich. Gepriesen gew├дhre du uns deine Arzeneien!

Grassmann

Wie auch das Kind sich dem verehrten Vater in Liebe zuneigt, wenn er kommt, o Rudra, So preis’ ich dich, den Herrn, der vieles schenket, gelobter du, verleih uns Arzeneien.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMaruts, I solicit of you those medicaments which are pure; those, showerers (of benefits), which give great plural asure; those which fonfer felicity; those which (our) sire, Manu, selected; and those (medicaments) of Rudra which are the alleviation (of disease), and defence (against danger).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those which our sire Manu selected: y─Бni manur avс╣Ыс╣З─лt─Б pit─Б naс╕е: Mah─Бbh─Бrata legend: reference to the vegetable seeds which Manu was directed to take with him into the vessel in which he was preserved at the time of the deluge

Jamison Brereton

Your gleaming remedies, o bullish Maruts, which bring best luck, which are joy itself,
which our father Manu choseтАФthose of RudraтАЩs do I want as luck and lifetime.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The ┼Ы├бс╣Г(tama)- here makes a ring with ┼Ы├бс╣Гtama- in 2a.

Note that in Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition the voc. vс╣Ыс╣гaс╣Зo is wrongly given as accented (vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гaс╣Зo).

Griffith

Of your pure medicines, O potent Martits, those that are wholesomest and healthbestowing,
Those which our father Manu hath selected, I crave from. Rudra for our gain and welfare.

Macdonell

Those remedies of yours, the pure, O Maruts, That are most wholesome, mighty ones, and potent, That Manu chose in ancient days, our Father: Those I desire, and Rudra’s balm and blessing.

Geldner

Eure lauteren Arzeneien, ihr Marut, die heilsamsten, ihr Bullen, die wohltuenden, die sich unser Vater Manu erbat, diese und Heil und Segen w├╝nsche ich von Rudra.

Grassmann

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the javelin of Rudra avoid us; may the great displeasure of the radiant deity pass away (from us); showerer of benefits, turn away your strong (bow) from the wealthy (offerers of oblations), and bestow happiness upon (our) sons and grandsons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 16.50: the end of the first half of the hymn reads: durmatir-agh─Бyoс╕е, the displeasure of the sinful or the malevolent; durmati-mah─л g─Бt = may the great displeasure pass away

Jamison Brereton

Might RudraтАЩs lance avoid us. The hostile thought of the turbulent one, though great, shall go around us.
Slacken the taut (bows) for our bounteous (patrons). Be merciful to our progeny and posterity, o munificent one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Ian Hollenbaugh pointed out to me, g─Бt in b should have a modal reading, either as an injunc. matching the precative value of the preceding verb vс╣Ыjy─Бс╕е or expressing the imperatival value often found in root aor. injunctives; hence either тАЬshould go around usтАЭ or тАЬlet it go around us.тАЭ The mid. impv. (├бva тАж) tanuс╣гva suggests that it is RudraтАЩs own bows that should be un-strung. Recall that he bore the bow in 10a (bibharс╣гi тАж dh├бnva).

Griffith

May Rudra’s missile turn aside and spare us, the great wrath of the impetuous One avoid us.
Turn, Bounteous God, thy strong bow from our princes, and be thou gracious to our seed and offspring.

Macdonell

May Rudra’s missile turn aside and pass us, May the fierce Rudra’s great ill-will go by us. Relax thy rigid bow to save our patrons; Spare, O thou god of bounty, child and grandchild.

Geldner

Das Gescho├Я des Rudra soll uns verschonen, die gro├Яe Ungnade des Furchtgebietenden soll uns umgehen. Entspanne die straffen Bogen unsern G├╢nnern zuliebe; sei gegen unseren leiblichen Samen barmherzig, du Belohner!

Grassmann

Des Rudra Wurfspiess geh’ an uns vor├╝ber, vor├╝ber auch des starken grosse Ungunst. O spanne deinen Bogen ab den F├╝rsten, o milder, sei den Kindern hold und Enkeln.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬCherisher of the world, showerer (of benefits), omniscient and divine (Rudra), hearer of our invocation, so consider us on this occasion, that you may not be irate, nor slay us; but that, blessed with excellent descendants, we may worthily glorify you at this sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You red-brown bull, constantly visibleтАФ(let it be) so, that you do not become angry, o god, and you do not smite.
Hearing our calls, be aware of us here, Rudra. тАУ May we speak loftily at the ritual distribution, in possession of good heroes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation, the y├бth─Б cl. is rendered as a purpose cl. (тАЬтАж that you do not become angry тАжтАЭ), but y├бth─Б purpose cls. always take the subjunctive, as Macdonell

already pointed out. It should rather be construed with the vs.-initial ev─Б╠Б, in the usual тАЬjust as тАж, so тАжтАЭ relationship, though with the usual order reversed. Macdonell also recognized this, but suggested that ev─Б╠Бis тАЬto be taken with c, since in the normal syntactical order if should follow y├бth─Б in the sense which it has here.тАЭ This is a trickier piece of syntax than I think can be justified тАФ hopscotching the ev─Б╠Бover the whole y├бth─Б clause тАФ and the contents of c do not conform to the standard usage of summary ev─Б╠Б. Instead I think ev─Б╠Бsums up the successful achievement of the wishes expressed in the preceding vs. (and perhaps in the whole preceding hymn): тАЬeven as you are not angry and do not smite, so (it is): the missile has avoided us, the bows are unstrung, etc.тАЭ This is somewhat hard to render in Engl., but I would change the published translation to тАЬJust as you are not angry and do not smite, so (it has come to pass).тАЭ

Griffith

O tawny Bull, thus showing forth thy nature, as neither to be wroth, O God, nor slay us.
Here, Rudra, listen to our invocation. Loud may we speak, with heroes, in assembly.

Macdonell

So brown-hued, mighty Rudra, widely famous, Here to our invocations be attentive, As not, O god, to rise in wrath and slay us. May we speak loud with heroes in the synod.

Geldner

So sei es, du rotbrauner, staunenerregender Bulle, da├Я du weder z├╝rnest noch t├╢test, o Gott. Sei hier, o Rudra, ein Ruferh├╢rer ! Wir m├╢chten das gro├Яe Wort f├╝hren als die Meister in der weisen Rede.

Grassmann

Als solcher dich, o brauner Stier, erweisend, der nicht, o Gott, du z├╝rnest, noch vertilgest, Sei unsres Rufs Erh├╢rer hier, o Rudra; lasst laut im Chore bei dem Fest uns singen.

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрде- рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреЗ рд╡реИрджреНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдЪреЗ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рдЕрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдиреЗ рдХреБрдгрд╛рдЪреЗ рдзрди рдШреЗрдК рдирдпреЗ. рдХреБрдгрд╛рдЪреЗ рд╣рдирди рдХрд░реВ рдирдпреЗ; рдкрд░рдВрддреБ рд╕рджреИрд╡ рдЪрд╛рдВрдЧрд▓реЗ рдкрдереНрдп рд╡ рдФрд╖рдзрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реЗрд╡рдирд╛рдиреЗ рдмрд▓ рд╡ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рд╡рд╛рдврд╡рд╛рд╡рд╛. рее резрел рее
